Definitions of Rasul and Nabi
Al-Bajuri defines 'rasul' and 'nabi' linguistically and technically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical definitions of a messenger (rasul) and a prophet (nabi), and the relationship between them.

Core Idea
Every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger.

Al-Bajuri begins by clarifying two key terms in prophethood: rasul and nabi. Understanding their precise definitions is essential to avoid confusion about the roles of prophets and messengers in Islam. This passage lays the foundation for distinguishing between them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the concise style of Al-Bajuri.
2
Identify the definitions of 'rasul'
Find the linguistic and technical definitions of 'rasul'. Note that the technical definition requires a command to convey the revelation.
3
Identify the definitions of 'nabi'
Similarly, find the definitions of 'nabi'. Observe that the technical definition does not require a command to convey; acting upon the revelation is sufficient.
4
Understand the relationship between them
Al-Bajuri states that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger. This is an absolute general-specific relationship (عموم وخصوص مطلق).
This is the well-known (mashhur) view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الرسول لغةً: المبعوث من مكان إلى آخر. واصطلاحاً: إنسان أُوحِيَ إليه بشرع يعمل به وأمر بتبليغه. وأما النبي؛ فهو لغةً: المُخْبِرُ بكسر الباء أو فتحها، فهو فعيل بمعنى فاعل أو مفعول واصطلاحاً: إنسان أوحي إليه بشرع يعمل به وإن لم يُؤْمَرُ بتبليغه فكلُّ رسول نبي ولا عكس فبينهما عموم وخصوص بإطلاق. هذا هو المشهور.
And know that 'al-rasul' (the messenger) linguistically: the one sent from one place to another. Technically: a human being who is revealed to with a law that he acts upon and is commanded to convey it. As for 'al-nabi' (the prophet), linguistically: the informer, with kasra of the ba or fatha, so it is on the pattern of 'fa'īl' in the sense of 'fā'il' or 'maf'ūl'. Technically: a human being who is revealed to with a law that he acts upon, even if he is not commanded to convey it. So every messenger is a prophet, but not vice versa. So between them is a general and specific relationship in an absolute sense. This is the well-known view.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage provides definitions of 'rasul' (messenger) and 'nabi' (prophet). Al-Bajuri first gives the linguistic definition of 'rasul': one sent from one place to another. The technical definition is a human being who receives revelation of a law, acts upon it, and is commanded to convey it. Then he defines 'nabi': linguistically, it means the informer (from the root naba'a), which can be read with kasra (mukhbir) or fatha (mukhbar), and is on the pattern of 'fa'īl' meaning either active or passive. Technically, a prophet is a human being who receives revelation of a law and acts upon it, even if he is not commanded to convey it. Al-Bajuri then states the relationship: every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger; thus there is a general-specific relationship (عموم وخصوص مطلق). This is the well-known (mashhur) view.

Key Terms
الرسول
النبي
الوحي
الشرع
التبليغ
الإنسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'prophet' and 'messenger' are identical or that all prophets must convey their message.
Correction: Al-Bajuri clarifies that a messenger is a prophet who is commanded to convey, while a prophet may not be commanded to convey.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between a messenger (rasul) and a prophet (nabi) according to Al-Bajuri?
A) They are identical
B) Every prophet is a messenger
C) Every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger
D) They are completely different

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is that a messenger is a prophet who is commanded to convey revelation, while a prophet may only be commanded to act upon it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that a prophet is one who acts upon revelation even if not commanded to convey. Ask yourself: Are you acting upon the knowledge you have from the Quran and Sunnah in your daily life, even if you don't teach others? What is one area where you fall short, and what will you change today?
?
The distinction between messenger and prophet shows that not every prophet is tasked with public proclamation. Yet you, as a follower of the final messenger, are commanded to convey what you know even if it is one verse. Are you fulfilling that duty? What holds you back from sharing the truth with those around you?
?
Al-Bajuri says that a messenger must convey the law. The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) conveyed the complete message. Does your life reflect that you have truly received and accepted that message? If you believe it is the truth, why do you not live as if it is the only thing that matters?

Distinguishing Rasul and Nabi
Defines rasul and nabi in language and terminology, states their general-specific relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between a messenger (rasul) and a prophet (nabi) in Islamic theology, and why every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa.

Core Idea
A messenger is a prophet with a mission to deliver.

In Islamic theology, the terms 'rasul' and 'nabi' are often used interchangeably in casual speech, but scholars make a precise distinction. This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin clarifies the linguistic and technical meanings of both terms and shows their logical relationship. Understanding this distinction is foundational for discussions about prophethood and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording introduce the definitions.
Notice the two parts of each definition: linguistic and technical.
2
Distinguish linguistic from technical definitions
Identify the linguistic meaning of rasul (one sent) and nabi (informer). Then compare with their technical meanings in Islamic law.
The technical definition is what actually matters for theology.
3
Understand the relationship
The passage concludes that every rasul is a nabi but not every nabi is a rasul. This is called 'general-specific absolute' (umum wa khusus mutlaq).
The key difference is the command to convey the revelation.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this distinction matters. It affects how we understand the roles of prophets and messengers in conveying divine law.
This distinction is often used in discussions about prophethood and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الرسول لغةً: المبعوث من مكان إلى آخر. واصطلاحاً: إنسان أُوحِيَ إليه بشرع يعمل به وأمر بتبليغه. وأما النبي؛ فهو لغةً: المُخْبِرُ بكسر الباء أو فتحها، فهو فعيل بمعنى فاعل أو مفعول واصطلاحاً: إنسان أوحي إليه بشرع يعمل به وإن لم يُؤْمَرُ بتبليغه فكلُّ رسول نبي ولا عكس فبينهما عموم وخصوص بإطلاق. هذا هو المشهور.
And know that the messenger (rasul) linguistically: the one sent from one place to another. And terminologically: a human being to whom a law is revealed to act upon and he is commanded to convey it. As for the prophet (nabi), he is linguistically: the informer (al-mukhbi) with kasr of the ba' or fath, so it is fa'il in the sense of fa'il or maf'ul. And terminologically: a human being to whom a law is revealed to act upon even if he is not commanded to convey it. So every messenger is a prophet and not vice versa, so between them is general-specific in an absolute sense. This is the well-known [view].
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the terms rasul and nabi. It first gives the linguistic meaning of rasul (sent from one place to another) and its technical meaning in Islamic terminology: a human being who receives revelation of a law, must act upon it, and is ordered to convey it. Then it defines nabi linguistically as an informer (derived from 'to inform', with two possible vowel patterns) and technically as a human being who receives revelation of a law to act upon, even if not ordered to convey it. From these definitions, it deduces the relationship: every rasul is a nabi, but not every nabi is a rasul. This is called 'general-specific in an absolute sense' (umum wa khusus mutlaq). The passage concludes that this is the well-known view.

Key Terms
رسول (Rasul)
نبي (Nabi)
عموم وخصوص مطلق (Umum wa Khusus Mutlaq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rasul and nabi are synonymous terms.
Correction: The passage shows that every rasul is a nabi, but not every nabi is a rasul. The difference is the command to convey revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the well-known view in this passage, what is the relationship between rasul and nabi?
A) Every nabi is a rasul
B) Every rasul is a nabi
C) They are synonymous
D) There is no relationship

Key Takeaway
Every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger; the key difference is the command to convey the revelation.

?
If you were a prophet but not a messenger, would you still feel compelled to share the revelation you received out of love for others? What does your answer reveal about your attitude toward obeying Allah's commands even when they aren't explicitly required?

Alternative Views on Rasul and Nabi and Definition of Caliph
Alternative views on rasul/nabi and definition of caliph with historical examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two alternative scholarly views on the relationship between rasul and nabi, the definition of a caliph as a prophet commanded to judge, and the historical succession of caliphs including the transition to kingship.

Core Idea
Rasul and nabi can be synonymous or intersect; a caliph is a prophet judging people.

This lesson presents two alternative views on the relationship between rasul and nabi beyond the earlier general-specific mutual. It then defines the caliph as a prophet commanded to judge among people, exemplified by Prophet David. The accompanying commentary clarifies the synonymous view and traces the historical caliphs from Abu Bakr to al-Hasan, explaining the transition to kingship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once. Notice the two phrases 'وقيل: إنهما مترادفان' and 'وبعضهم يَجْعَلُ بينهما عموماً وخصوصاً' indicating alternative views.
The passage also includes a commentary section.
2
Grasp the alternative views
Identify the two views: they are synonymous (mutaradifan) and they have a general-specific from one perspective (umum wa khusus min wajh). Understand the condition mentioned for the second view that the prophet must be distinguished by some rulings.
3
Understand the definition of caliph
Locate the sentence defining caliph: 'ومتى أُمِرَ بالحكم بين الناس؛ فخليفة'. Relate it to the Quranic verse about David.
The caliph is not a separate category but a function of a prophet.
4
Follow the commentary
Read the commentary section that clarifies the meaning of 'synonymous' and then lists the caliphs: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, and al-Hasan. Note the concept of 'ملك عضوض' (biting kingship).
The commentary also explains al-Hasan's abdication to Mu'awiya.
5
Reflect on the timeline
Understand that the caliphate lasted 30 years, ending with al-Hasan, after which it became kingship. Consider why al-Hasan gave up the caliphate to preserve Muslim unity.
This is based on the hadith cited in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل: إنهما مترادفان، وبعضهم يَجْعَلُ بينهما عموماً وخصوصاً من وجه بناءً على أنه يُشْتَرَطُ في النبي: أن يختص بأحكام؛ لأنهما حينئذ يجتمعان فيمن أمر بتبليغ بعض الأحكام واختص ببعضها الآخر، وينفرد الرسول فيمن أُمِرَ بتبليغ الكل، وينفرد النبي فيمن اختص بالكل. ومتى أُمِرَ بالحكم بين الناس؛ فخليفة كما قال تعالى: ﴿ يَا دَاوُدُ إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ الآية. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري: (قوله مُتَرَادِفَانِ) أي: على معنى الرسول كما في "شرح الشنشوري على الرحبية". تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. ولك أن تمنع أن هنا إظهاراً في مقام الإضمار؛ لأنه لا يكون إلا في جملة واحدة، وما هنا ليس كذلك كما نُقِلَ عن الشَّبْرَامُلسِي. And it is said: They are synonymous. And some make between them a general-specific from one perspective based on the condition that the prophet must be distinguished by rulings; because then they meet in the one who is commanded to convey some rulings and distinguished by some others, and the messenger is unique in the one commanded to convey all, and the prophet is unique in the one distinguished by all. And when he is commanded to judge among people, he is a caliph, as the Most High said: {O David, indeed We have made you a caliph on the earth} — the verse. Commentary of al-Allama Ahmad al-Ujhuri: (His saying: 'synonymous') meaning: with the meaning of the messenger as in Sharh al-Shanshuri on al-Rahbiyya. Taqrirat of al-Allama Muhammad al-Anbabi. And you may deny that here there is a making explicit in place of pronominalization, because it only occurs in one sentence, and this is not like that as transmitted from al-Shabramallisi. (His saying: 'And it is said: They are synonymous') meaning: with the meaning of the prophet preceding, as is apparent. (His saying: 'caliph') And the Prophet of Allah was also described with it, and after him it was for Abu Bakr, then for Umar, then for Uthman, then for Ali, and when Ali died, the people pledged allegiance to his son al-Hasan, so he became a true caliph for a period of six months, completing the thirty years which the Prophet of Allah informed is the period of the caliphate, then there will be a biting kingship, i.e., people bite it due to the injustice of its people and their lack of uprightness. And when that period ended, he gave up the caliphate to Mu'awiya out of asceticism and to protect the blood of Muslims, for more than forty thousand pledged allegiance to him, and this is the fulfillment of his saying, "And perhaps Allah will bring about peace through him between two great groups of Muslims."
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents two alternative views on the relationship between rasul and nabi beyond the well-known general-specific mutual. First, some say they are synonymous (mutaradifan). Second, some hold a different kind of general-specific from one perspective (umum wa khusus min wajh), which is explained by a condition: if the nabi must be distinguished by some rulings (i.e., is assigned something not given to others), then the two terms can intersect. In this view, they meet in someone who is commanded to convey only some rulings and is distinguished by others; the rasul is unique in conveying all; the nabi is unique in being distinguished by all. The passage then defines the caliph: when a prophet or nabi is commanded to judge among people, he is a caliph, supported by the Quranic verse to David. The subsequent commentary from al-Ujhuri clarifies the meaning of 'synonymous' in this context, and adds a note that the izhar (explicit mention) that had been discussed earlier is not problematic because it occurs in one sentence. Finally, the commentary expands on the caliphate, listing the rightly guided caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) and adding al-Hasan ibn Ali, explaining that his six-month caliphate completed the thirty-year period predicted by the Prophet, after which kingship that bites (due to injustice) would follow. It also mentions al-Hasan's abdication to Mu'awiya to preserve unity, citing the hadith about peace between two great groups.

Correction: The passage includes al-Hasan ibn Ali as a rightful caliph for six months, completing the thirty-year caliphate, after which it became kingship.

Linguistic and Legal Definitions of Tawhid
Sanusi enumerates three definitions of tawhid: linguistic, technical as a science, and technical as worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and two technical definitions of tawhid as given by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Tawhid means knowing oneness, but technically it is either a science of proofs or worshipping God alone.

Sanusi begins by grounding the concept of tawhid in language and sacred law. The linguistic definition is simple, but the technical meanings open two distinct dimensions: one as a systematic science (ilm al-kalam) and the other as the actual act of devotion. Understanding these distinctions is essential before studying the proofs of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the three separate definitions presented.
The text is concise; each definition is introduced by a key word (لغةً, شرعاً, وقيل).
2
Identify the three definitions
Locate the linguistic definition, the technical definition as a science, and the technical definition as an act of worship. Also note the additional definition starting with 'وقيل'.
The second definition (as a science) is the basis for the entire field of kalam.
3
Reflect on the distinction between the two technical meanings
Consider how the science of kalam differs from the act of worship. The science is about proofs and certainty, while the worship is about singling out God in devotion.
Both are called tawhid but refer to different aspects.
4
Understand the alternative definition
Read the definition 'affirmation of an essence not resembling essences nor emptied of attributes'. This emphasizes God's uniqueness and attributes.
This definition combines negation of similitude and affirmation of attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن أم البراهين لأبي عبد الله السنوسي فحده لغةً: العِلْمُ بأن الشيء واحد. وشرعاً بمعنى الفن المدون: عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن إثبات العقائد الدينية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية، وبغير معنى الفن المدوّن: إفراد المعبود بالعبادة مع اعتقاد وخدته ذاتاً وصفات وأفعالاً. وقيل: إثباتُ ذاتٍ غيرِ مُشْبِهَةٍ للذوات ولا معطلة عن الصفات. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: عِلْمٌ) أي: قضايا بدليل قوله : (يبحث فيه)؛ إذ المبحوث فيه هو القضايا. (وقوله: عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ المراد به الثبوت لا إدراكه؛ لأن نتيجة الدليل ثبوت العقيدة لا إدراك ثبوتها. (وقوله: الْمُكْتَسَب) صفة للإثبات بمعنى الثبوت. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. (قوله: عِلْمَ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ... إلخ) حَدَّهُ غيره : بأنه عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن ذات الله من حيث إنها قديمةً مخالفة للحوادث... إلخ، وعن صِفَاتِه من حيث تقسيمها لنفسي وسلبي ومعان ومعنوية، ومتعلّقة وغير متعلّقة، والمتعلّق عام التعلق وخاصه، وقديمه وحادثه كما في صفات الأفعال عند الأشعري إلى غير ذلك، وعن أحوال الممكنات في المَبْدَأ من حيث إنها حادثة ناشئة بالاختيار لا بالتعليل والمَعَاد من حيث الحشرُ وبقيَّةُ السمعيات على قانون الإسلام - أي: قواعده غير المصادمة للشرع .. فخرج إلهيات الفلاسفة، فإنها مُجَرَّدُ تخيل، وبَقِيَتِ النبوَّاتُ، فإما أن يُعْتَبَرَ إدراجها في أحوال الممكنات، وإما في الصفات من حيث إن الإرسال من صفات الأفعال. وأما نحو مَبْحَثِ نَصْبِ الإمام وتقليد الأئمة؛ فإنما ذُكِرَ في بعض كُتُبِ هذا الفنّ لكثرة ضلال الفرق الزَّائِغَةِ فيه. وحده أيضاً: بأنه عِلْمٌ يُقْتَدَرُ معه على إثبات العقائد الدينية على الغير، وإلزامها إياه بإيراد الحُجَج، ودفع الشُبَه. وعرفه الشعدُ بقوله: العلم بالعقائد الدينية الناشئ عن الأدلة اليقينية. (قوله: إِفْرَادُ الْمَعْبُودِ... إلخ) يعني: عَدَمُ الشريك عَبَدَه بالفعل أو لا؛ إذ فعل العبادة ليس شرطاً في التوحيد.
The text of Umm al-Barahin by Abu Abdullah al-Sanusi: So its definition linguistically: the knowledge that a thing is one. And legally, in the sense of the codified art: a science in which is investigated the establishment of religious beliefs acquired from their certain proofs. And in other than the sense of the codified art: singling out the worshipped with worship together with belief in His oneness in essence, attributes, and actions. And it was said: the affirmation of an essence not resembling essences nor emptied of attributes. The gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: His saying: 'a science' - meaning propositions, evidenced by his saying: 'is investigated in it', since what is investigated is the propositions. And his saying: 'about the establishment' - what is intended by it is the certainty (thubut), not the perception of it, because the result of the proof is the certainty of the creed, not the perception of its certainty. And his saying: 'acquired' - is an adjective for 'establishment' in the sense of 'certainty'. The taqrirat of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi: His saying: 'a science in which is investigated... etc.' - Others defined it as: a science in which is investigated about the essence of God insofar as it is eternal, contrary to contingent things... etc., and about His attributes in terms of their division into self, negative, meanings, and meaning-related, and related and non-related, and the related being general in relation and specific, and eternal and contingent as in the attributes of actions according to al-Ash'ari, etc., and about the states of contingent things in the beginning insofar as they are contingent and arise by choice not by causation, and the Return (ma'ad) in terms of the gathering and the rest of the sam'iyyat (matters of revelation) according to the law of Islam - i.e., its rules not conflicting with the Shari'a. Thus the theology of the philosophers is excluded, for it is mere delusion. And the prophecies remain; either considered included in the states of contingent things, or in the attributes insofar as sending is among the attributes of actions. As for the discussion of the appointment of the imam and the following of imams, it is only mentioned in some books of this art due to the great misguidance of the deviant sects concerning it. And it was also defined as: a science by which one is able to establish religious beliefs upon others and compel them to them by presenting proofs and refuting doubts. And al-Sa'd defined it as: the knowledge of religious beliefs arising from certain proofs. His saying: 'singling out the worshipped... etc.' - meaning the absence of a partner, whether he worships Him actually or not, since the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the linguistic and legal definitions of tawhid, along with alternative definitions of the science of kalam and clarifying commentary. The main text by Sanusi first gives the linguistic definition of tawhid: 'the knowledge that a thing is one.' Legally (شرعا), it has two senses. First, as the codified art (الفن المدون), it is 'a science in which is investigated the establishment of religious beliefs acquired from their certain proofs'—this is the definition of 'ilm al-kalam. Second, in the sense other than the codified art, tawhid is 'singling out the worshipped with worship together with belief in His oneness in essence, attributes, and actions.' Another definition is also given: 'the affirmation of an essence not resembling essences nor emptied of attributes.' Al-Ajhuri's gloss explains parts of the first definition: 'a science' means propositions (قضايا), since what is investigated is propositions; 'about the establishment' (إثبات) means the certainty (ثبوت) of the creed, not the perception of it, because the proof results in the creed being certain, not in our perceiving that certainty; and 'acquired' (مكتسب) is an adjective for 'establishment' meaning 'certainty' (ثبوت). Al-Anbabi's taqrirat then expands on the definition of kalam, citing other definitions: it investigates God's essence (ذات الله) insofar as it is eternal and contrary to contingents, and His attributes divided into various categories, and the states of contingent beings in the beginning (المبدأ) as arising by choice, and the Return (المعاد) regarding the resurrection and other sam'iyyat—these are according to Islamic law, excluding the philosophers' theology. Prophecies are either included under states of contingent things or attributes. The discussion of the imam and following imams is included only due to sectarian deviations. Finally, another definition is given: a science enabling one to establish beliefs on others by proofs and rebutting doubts, and al-Sa'd's definition: 'knowledge of religious beliefs arising from certain proofs.' The last comment clarifies that 'singling out the worshipped' means the absence of a partner, regardless of actual performance of worship, since the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.

Key Terms
التوحيد
علم الكلام
عقائد
أدلة يقينية
الفن المدون
إفراد المعبود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think tawhid only means saying 'God is one' verbally without deeper understanding or action.
Correction: Sanusi shows that tawhid has multiple dimensions: it is a science requiring proofs, and it is an act of worship involving belief in oneness of essence, attributes, and actions.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the technical definition of التوحيد (tawhid) when meant as the codified science (الفن المدون)?
A) The knowledge that God is one.
B) A science that investigates the establishment of religious beliefs acquired from their certain proofs.
C) The act of singling out God in worship with belief in His oneness.
D) The affirmation of an essence not resembling essences.

Key Takeaway
Tawhid has both a linguistic meaning (knowing something is one) and two technical meanings: as a science of proofs for beliefs and as the act of worshipping God alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three definitions of tawhid do you find yourself neglecting in your daily life: knowing that God is one, proving His attributes through evidence, or directing all worship to Him alone? How will you rebalance your focus starting today?
?
The linguistic definition says tawhid is 'knowledge that a thing is one.' Are you truly convinced in your heart that nothing else deserves your ultimate trust and fear besides God? What competing 'gods'—like status, comfort, or relationships—still divide your heart, and what concrete step will you take this week to dethrone them?
?
Sanusi mentions affirming an essence that does not resemble anything and is not devoid of attributes. When you imagine God, do you unconsciously picture Him like something you know? How will you train your mind to uphold both His transcendence and His attribute-filled reality in your worship?

Definition and Scope of Ilm al-Kalam
Commentary on the definition of ilm al-kalam, clarifying terms and presenting its subject matter and alternative definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentary expands the definition of ilm al-kalam, including its subject matter and purpose.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam is the science of proofs for religious beliefs, covering God, attributes, and the afterlife.

After the main text defines tawhid as a science, the glosses clarify technical terms and present alternative definitions. Al-Anbabi's taqrirat details the subjects investigated: God's essence and attributes, the origin of contingent things, and the Return (ma'ad). This lesson unpacks these expansions to give a fuller picture of what the science of kalam entails.

Guided Path
1
Read the commentary passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the glosses. Notice that it begins by explaining words in the definition ('علم', 'إثبات', 'مكتسب').
The gloss is from al-Ajhuri and al-Anbabi, building on Sanusi's text.
2
Understand the clarification of terms
Al-Ajhuri explains that 'علم' means propositions (قضايا), and 'إثبات' means certainty (ثبوت), not perception. This refines the definition.
The result of proof is that the creed is certain, not that we perceive its certainty.
3
Identify the detailed subject matter
Al-Anbabi lists what kalam investigates: God's essence, attributes (divided into categories), states of contingent beings, and the Return (resurrection).
This shows kalam covers both divine and eschatological topics.
4
Recognize alternative definitions
The passage gives three more definitions: a comprehensive one by 'others', a functional one (ability to establish beliefs on others), and al-Sa'd's definition.
These emphasize either the content or the purpose of the science.
5
Reflect on the final clarification about tawhid
The passage ends by noting that 'singling out the worshipped' means no partner, regardless of actual worship performed.
This links back to the definition of tawhid as an act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن أم البراهين لأبي عبد الله السنوسي فحده لغةً: العِلْمُ بأن الشيء واحد. وشرعاً بمعنى الفن المدون: عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن إثبات العقائد الدينية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية، وبغير معنى الفن المدوّن: إفراد المعبود بالعبادة مع اعتقاد وخدته ذاتاً وصفات وأفعالاً. وقيل: إثباتُ ذاتٍ غيرِ مُشْبِهَةٍ للذوات ولا معطلة عن الصفات. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: عِلْمٌ) أي: قضايا بدليل قوله : (يبحث فيه)؛ إذ المبحوث فيه هو القضايا. (وقوله: عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ المراد به الثبوت لا إدراكه؛ لأن نتيجة الدليل ثبوت العقيدة لا إدراك ثبوتها. (وقوله: الْمُكْتَسَب) صفة للإثبات بمعنى الثبوت. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. (قوله: عِلْمَ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ... إلخ) حَدَّهُ غيره : بأنه عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن ذات الله من حيث إنها قديمةً مخالفة للحوادث... إلخ، وعن صِفَاتِه من حيث تقسيمها لنفسي وسلبي ومعان ومعنوية، ومتعلّقة وغير متعلّقة، والمتعلّق عام التعلق وخاصه، وقديمه وحادثه كما في صفات الأفعال عند الأشعري إلى غير ذلك، وعن أحوال الممكنات في المَبْدَأ من حيث إنها حادثة ناشئة بالاختيار لا بالتعليل والمَعَاد من حيث الحشرُ وبقيَّةُ السمعيات على قانون الإسلام - أي: قواعده غير المصادمة للشرع .. فخرج إلهيات الفلاسفة، فإنها مُجَرَّدُ تخيل، وبَقِيَتِ النبوَّاتُ، فإما أن يُعْتَبَرَ إدراجها في أحوال الممكنات، وإما في الصفات من حيث إن الإرسال من صفات الأفعال. وأما نحو مَبْحَثِ نَصْبِ الإمام وتقليد الأئمة؛ فإنما ذُكِرَ في بعض كُتُبِ هذا الفنّ لكثرة ضلال الفرق الزَّائِغَةِ فيه. وحده أيضاً: بأنه عِلْمٌ يُقْتَدَرُ معه على إثبات العقائد الدينية على الغير، وإلزامها إياه بإيراد الحُجَج، ودفع الشُبَه. وعرفه الشعدُ بقوله: العلم بالعقائد الدينية الناشئ عن الأدلة اليقينية. (قوله: إِفْرَادُ الْمَعْبُودِ... إلخ) يعني: عَدَمُ الشريك عَبَدَه بالفعل أو لا؛ إذ فعل العبادة ليس شرطاً في التوحيد.
The text of Umm al-Barahin by Abu Abdullah al-Sanusi: So its definition linguistically: the knowledge that a thing is one. And legally, in the sense of the codified art: a science in which is investigated the establishment of religious beliefs acquired from their certain proofs. And in other than the sense of the codified art: singling out the worshipped with worship together with belief in His oneness in essence, attributes, and actions. And it was said: the affirmation of an essence not resembling essences nor emptied of attributes. The gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: His saying: 'a science' - meaning propositions, evidenced by his saying: 'is investigated in it', since what is investigated is the propositions. And his saying: 'about the establishment' - what is intended by it is the certainty (thubut), not the perception of it, because the result of the proof is the certainty of the creed, not the perception of its certainty. And his saying: 'acquired' - is an adjective for 'establishment' in the sense of 'certainty'. The taqrirat of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi: His saying: 'a science in which is investigated... etc.' - Others defined it as: a science in which is investigated about the essence of God insofar as it is eternal, contrary to contingent things... etc., and about His attributes in terms of their division into self, negative, meanings, and meaning-related, and related and non-related, and the related being general in relation and specific, and eternal and contingent as in the attributes of actions according to al-Ash'ari, etc., and about the states of contingent things in the beginning insofar as they are contingent and arise by choice not by causation, and the Return (ma'ad) in terms of the gathering and the rest of the sam'iyyat (matters of revelation) according to the law of Islam - i.e., its rules not conflicting with the Shari'a. Thus the theology of the philosophers is excluded, for it is mere delusion. And the prophecies remain; either considered included in the states of contingent things, or in the attributes insofar as sending is among the attributes of actions. As for the discussion of the appointment of the imam and the following of imams, it is only mentioned in some books of this art due to the great misguidance of the deviant sects concerning it. And it was also defined as: a science by which one is able to establish religious beliefs upon others and compel them to them by presenting proofs and refuting doubts. And al-Sa'd defined it as: the knowledge of religious beliefs arising from certain proofs. His saying: 'singling out the worshipped... etc.' - meaning the absence of a partner, whether he worships Him actually or not, since the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the linguistic and legal definitions of tawhid, along with alternative definitions of the science of kalam and clarifying commentary. The main text by Sanusi first gives the linguistic definition of tawhid: 'the knowledge that a thing is one.' Legally (شرعا), it has two senses. First, as the codified art (الفن المدون), it is 'a science in which is investigated the establishment of religious beliefs acquired from their certain proofs'—this is the definition of 'ilm al-kalam. Second, in the sense other than the codified art, tawhid is 'singling out the worshipped with worship together with belief in His oneness in essence, attributes, and actions.' Another definition is also given: 'the affirmation of an essence not resembling essences nor emptied of attributes.' Al-Ajhuri's gloss explains parts of the first definition: 'a science' means propositions (قضايا), since what is investigated is propositions; 'about the establishment' (إثبات) means the certainty (ثبوت) of the creed, not the perception of it, because the proof results in the creed being certain, not in our perceiving that certainty; and 'acquired' (مكتسب) is an adjective for 'establishment' meaning 'certainty' (ثبوت). Al-Anbabi's taqrirat then expands on the definition of kalam, citing other definitions: it investigates God's essence (ذات الله) insofar as it is eternal and contrary to contingents, and His attributes divided into various categories, and the states of contingent beings in the beginning (المبدأ) as arising by choice, and the Return (المعاد) regarding the resurrection and other sam'iyyat—these are according to Islamic law, excluding the philosophers' theology. Prophecies are either included under states of contingent things or attributes. The discussion of the imam and following imams is included only due to sectarian deviations. Finally, another definition is given: a science enabling one to establish beliefs on others by proofs and rebutting doubts, and al-Sa'd's definition: 'knowledge of religious beliefs arising from certain proofs.' The last comment clarifies that 'singling out the worshipped' means the absence of a partner, regardless of actual performance of worship, since the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think ilm al-kalam is only about abstract theology without practical purpose.
Correction: The commentary shows kalam has a functional purpose: establishing beliefs on others and refuting doubts, as well as covering practical topics like imamah.

Checkpoint
According to al-Anbabi's taqrirat, which of the following is NOT included in the detailed subject matter of ilm al-kalam?
A) The essence of God as eternal and unlike contingents.
B) The division of God's attributes into various categories.
C) The states of contingent beings in the beginning (المبدأ).
D) The natural sciences like physics and biology.

Key Takeaway
Ilm al-kalam is a science that investigates God's essence and attributes, the states of contingent beings, and the Return, using certain proofs to establish religious beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the core beliefs of your faith as certainties established by proof, or do you merely accept them as inherited assumptions? What would change if you pursued certainty like the scholars of kalam?
?
The passage distinguishes between the objective certainty of a creed and our perception of it. In your own life, is your conviction in tawhid based on what is objectively true, or on your own subjective feeling? How would you test the difference?
?
If ilm al-kalam includes investigating the states of contingent beings, do you live with a conscious awareness that you are entirely contingent upon God every moment? How does that awareness shape your daily choices and reliance on Him?

Defining Ilm al-Kalam: The Science of Religious Beliefs
Sanusi defines ilm al-kalam technically and al-Ajhuri clarifies the key terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the technical definition of ilm al-kalam as a discipline and the precise meanings of its key terms like 'science', 'establishment', and 'acquired'.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam is the science of establishing religious beliefs from certain proofs.

Before diving into theological arguments, a clear definition of the discipline itself is essential. In this passage, Sanusi gives the technical definition of ilm al-kalam, and al-Ajhuri unpacks each term to remove ambiguity. Understanding these distinctions is the first step in mastering kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a linguistic definition before moving to the technical.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find the linguistic definition (knowledge that something is one) and the technical definition (a science investigating the establishment of religious beliefs from certain proofs).
The technical definition is the focus of the lesson.
3
Examine the three clarifications
Al-Ajhuri clarifies three points: (1) 'science' means propositions, (2) 'establishment' means the actual establishment (not perception of it), and (3) 'acquired' describes establishment. Notice how each clarification refines the definition.
These clarifications prevent common misunderstandings.
4
Reflect on the key terms
Consider why it matters that 'establishment' (إثبات) refers to the belief being established, not the act of proving. This distinction is critical for understanding the goal of kalam.
The result of proof is the certainty of the belief itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فحده لغةً: العِلْمُ بأن الشيء واحد. وشرعاً بمعنى الفن المدون: عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن إثبات العقائد الدينية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية.
(قوله: عِلْمٌ) أي: قضايا بدليل قوله : (يبحث فيه)؛ إذ المبحوث فيه هو القضايا.
(وقوله: عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ المراد به الثبوت لا إدراكه؛ لأن نتيجة الدليل ثبوت العقيدة لا إدراك ثبوتها.
(وقوله: الْمُكْتَسَب) صفة للإثبات بمعنى الثبوت.
So its definition linguistically: knowledge that something is one. And legislatively, in the sense of the codified discipline: a science in which investigation is made about the establishment of religious beliefs, acquired from certain proofs. (His saying: 'a science') means: propositions, evidenced by his saying: 'investigation is made in it'; for the investigated matters are the propositions. (And his saying: 'about the establishment') what is meant by it is the establishment itself, not the perception of it; because the result of the proof is the establishment of the belief, not the perception of its establishment. (And his saying: 'acquired') is an attribute of establishment in the sense of being established.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage defines the science of kalam. It begins with the linguistic definition of tawhid, then gives the technical definition of kalam as a discipline: a science that investigates the establishment of religious beliefs from certain proofs. The commentary by al-Ajhuri clarifies three points: First, 'science' refers to propositions, because what is investigated are propositions. Second, 'establishment' (إثبات) means the actual establishment of the belief, not the perception of that establishment, because the proof yields the establishment itself. Third, 'acquired' is an attribute of 'establishment,' meaning the belief is established through the proof.

إثبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'إثبات' refers to the act of proving or the perception of establishment.
Correction: Al-Ajhuri clarifies that 'إثبات' means the actual establishment (ثبوت) of the belief in the mind, not the act of proving or the perception of that establishment. The proof results in the belief being established.

Checkpoint

B) The establishment (إثبات)
C) The proof (دليل)
D) The belief (عقيدة)

Key Takeaway
The technical definition of ilm al-kalam focuses on the certain establishment of religious beliefs through proof, and each term in the definition carries a precise meaning that prevents misinterpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that ilm al-kalam aims at the establishment of beliefs from certain proofs, not just knowing the proofs. Are the beliefs you hold about Allah firmly established in your heart, or do you only have intellectual arguments without conviction? What step will you take today to move from argument to establishment?
?
The definition says the establishment is 'acquired' – it is not simply inherited or absorbed from your environment. Are you actively acquiring certainty in your faith, or are you relying on what you grew up with? Will you commit to studying proofs for your beliefs until they become personally established?
?
If someone asked you to prove that God exists and that Islam is true, could you produce a certain proof from the sources? Or would you realize that your belief is not yet fully established? What will you do about that gap starting today?

Alternative Definitions of Kalam by Al-Anbabi
Al-Anbabi presents multiple definitions of ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various alternative definitions of ilm al-kalam provided by Al-Anbabi, including their scope and exclusions.

Core Idea
Kalam is defined not only by its subject but also by its purpose and method.

Al-Anbabi's notes offer a richer picture of what ilm al-kalam encompasses. While the matn gives a concise definition, these alternatives expand on the details, including what is studied and what is excluded. This lesson explores these definitions to deepen your understanding of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative definitions
Read the passage from Al-Anbabi, noting each definition and its key elements.
Notice the structure: first definition with subpoints, then exclusions, then additional definitions.
2
Understand the first definition's scope
The first definition covers God's essence, attributes, states of contingent beings, and sam'iyyat. Observe the detailed divisions of attributes.
3
Identify what is excluded
The metaphysics of philosophers are explicitly excluded. Consider why this distinction is important.
The passage says philosopher's metaphysics are 'mere imagination'.
4
Compare the practical definition
The second definition focuses on establishing beliefs for others through arguments. Compare this with the first definition's subject matter.
This highlights the dual nature of kalam: theoretical and practical.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Al-Sha'd's definition ties kalam to certain proofs. Think about how all definitions together frame the discipline.

Source Text

تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي.
(قوله: عِلْمَ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ... إلخ) حَدَّهُ غيره : بأنه عِلْمٌ يُبْحَثُ فيه عن ذات الله من حيث إنها قديمةً مخالفة للحوادث... إلخ، وعن صِفَاتِه من حيث تقسيمها لنفسي وسلبي ومعان ومعنوية، ومتعلّقة وغير متعلّقة، والمتعلّق عام التعلق وخاصه، وقديمه وحادثه كما في صفات الأفعال عند الأشعري إلى غير ذلك، وعن أحوال الممكنات في المَبْدَأ من حيث إنها حادثة ناشئة بالاختيار لا بالتعليل والمَعَاد من حيث الحشرُ وبقيَّةُ السمعيات على قانون الإسلام - أي: قواعده غير المصادمة للشرع ..
فخرج إلهيات الفلاسفة، فإنها مُجَرَّدُ تخيل، وبَقِيَتِ النبوَّاتُ، فإما أن يُعْتَبَرَ إدراجها في أحوال الممكنات، وإما في الصفات من حيث إن الإرسال من صفات الأفعال. وأما نحو مَبْحَثِ نَصْبِ الإمام وتقليد الأئمة؛ فإنما ذُكِرَ في بعض كُتُبِ هذا الفنّ لكثرة ضلال الفرق الزَّائِغَةِ فيه.
وحده أيضاً: بأنه عِلْمٌ يُقْتَدَرُ معه على إثبات العقائد الدينية على الغير، وإلزامها إياه بإيراد الحُجَج، ودفع الشُّبَه. وعرفه الشعدُ بقوله: العلم بالعقائد الدينية الناشئ عن الأدلة اليقينية.
The notes of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi. (His saying: 'a science in which investigation is made... etc.') Someone else defined it as: a science in which investigation is made about the essence of God, in that it is eternal, unlike contingent beings... etc., and about His attributes in terms of their division into essential, negative, meanings, and meaningful, and related and unrelated, and the related general and specific, and eternal and temporal as in the attributes of actions according to al-Ash'ari, and so on, and about the states of contingent beings in the beginning in that they are temporal and arise by choice, not by causation, and about the Return in terms of resurrection and the rest of the sam'iyyat according to the law of Islam—i.e., its rules that do not conflict with revelation. Thus the metaphysics of the philosophers are excluded, for they are mere imagination. The discussions of prophethood remain; either they are considered included in the states of contingent beings, or in the attributes in that sending is among the attributes of actions. As for topics like the appointment of an imam and following the imams, they are mentioned in some books of this discipline due to the great misguidance of the deviant sects in that matter. He also defined it: as a science by which one is able to establish religious beliefs for others and impose them upon them by presenting arguments and refuting doubts. And al-Sha'd defined it as: knowledge of religious beliefs arising from certain proofs.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from al-Anbabi's notes offers alternative definitions of kalam that are more detailed than the matn. It specifies the subject as God's essence and attributes, the states of contingent beings, and sam'iyyat, while excluding the metaphysics of philosophers. It also includes a definition emphasizing the ability to establish beliefs for others and a definition by al-Sha'd as knowledge from certain proofs. The passage shows the diversity in defining kalam while maintaining the centrality of certain proofs.

Definition of Tawhid in the General Sense
Sanusi defines tawhid outside the discipline and al-Ajhuri comments on worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general definition of tawhid and the distinction between belief in oneness and the physical act of worship.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the absence of a partner, not the act of worship itself.

This lesson unpacks the definition of tawhid outside the specialized discipline of kalam. Sanusi presents two formulations, and al-Ajhuri clarifies a common misunderstanding about worship. As you read, notice how the definitions emphasize belief and essence rather than ritual actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let Sanusi's wording sink in before analyzing.
The passage contains two distinct definitions.
2
Identify the two definitions
Notice the first definition: 'إفراد المعبود بالعبادة مع اعتقاد وحدته'. Then 'وقيل' introduces a second definition focusing on essence not resembling others nor devoid of attributes.
The second definition is more philosophical.
3
Understand the commentary
Al-Ajhuri explains that 'singling out the worshipped' means the absence of a partner, whether or not one actually performs worship. Worship is not a condition for tawhid.
This guards against confusing tawhid with its outward manifestation.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself: why is it important that tawhid is defined as belief and absence of a partner rather than as an action? Think about someone who believes but cannot perform worship.
This connects to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبغير معنى الفن المدوّن: إفراد المعبود بالعبادة مع اعتقاد وحدته ذاتاً وصفات وأفعالاً. وقيل: إثباتُ ذاتٍ غيرِ مُشْبِهَةٍ للذوات ولا معطلة عن الصفات.
(قوله: إِفْرَادُ الْمَعْبُودِ... إلخ) يعني: عَدَمُ الشريك عَبَدَه بالفعل أو لا؛ إذ فعل العبادة ليس شرطاً في التوحيد.
And in the sense other than the codified discipline: singling out the worshipped one by worship while believing in His unity in essence, attributes, and actions. And it is said: establishing an essence that does not resemble essences nor is stripped of attributes. (His saying: 'singling out the worshipped... etc.') means: the absence of a partner, whether one has actually worshipped Him or not; for the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage defines tawhid in the general sense, not as a discipline. It means worshipping God alone while believing in His unity. The commentary clarifies that the definition does not require actual worship; rather, it is the belief in God's oneness and the absence of partners. A secondary definition is also given: establishing an essence that is neither similar to other essences nor devoid of attributes, emphasizing God's transcendence and possession of attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawhid requires actually performing acts of worship; without worship, one is not a muwahhid.
Correction: According to the commentary, tawhid is essentially the absence of a partner in belief, not dependent on performing worship. The act of worship is not a condition for tawhid.

Checkpoint

A) Actually worshipping Him
B) The absence of a partner
C) Believing in His attributes only
D) Abstaining from worship

Key Takeaway
The essence of tawhid is the absence of any partner in worship, not the physical act of worship itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that your prayers and rituals are enough to define your tawhid, while your heart secretly attaches importance to other things? What would it mean for you to truly have no partner in your worship, even in your innermost thoughts?
?
If tawhid is about the absence of a partner, then what are the hidden partners in your life—people, status, comforts—that you rely on as if they were deities? Today, what step will you take to remove them from your heart?
?
The lesson says the act of worship is not a condition for tawhid; rather, it is the belief. How does that challenge the way you measure your faith? Are you more concerned with performing acts or with the conviction in your heart?

The Subject and Fruit of 'Ilm al-Kalam
Sanusi defines the subject and benefit of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise subject matter of 'ilm al-kalam and its ultimate benefit.

Core Idea
Kalam studies Allah and His messenger, using contingency proofs and revealed truths.

Sanusi begins his definition of kalam by identifying what it studies and why it matters. The subject is not just God in isolation, but also His messenger and the entire framework of necessary, impossible, and possible attributes. The benefit is no less than eternal happiness through decisive knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once. Notice the terms 'wajib', 'mustahil', 'ja'iz' in relation to Allah and His messenger.
These three categories are foundational.
2
Identify the components of the subject
The subject includes four elements: the essence of Allah, the essence of the Prophet, the contingent as evidence, and transmitted matters as beliefs.
3
Understand the fruit
The fruit (thamara) is knowledge through decisive proofs and attainment of eternal happiness. Reflect on why this is the highest benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وموضوعه ذات الله وذاتُ رسوله من حيث ما يَجِبُ، وما يستحيل، وما يجوز، والممكنُ من حيث إنه يُسْتَدَلَّ به على وجود صانعه، والسمعيات من حيث اعتقادها. وثمرتُه معرفةُ صفات الله ورسله بالبراهين القطعية والفوز بالسعادة الأبدية. وفضله أنه أشرفُ العلوم لكونه متعلقاً بذات الله تعالى وذات رُسُله وما يتبع ذلك، والمتعلّق يشْرُفُ بشَرَف المتعلق. ونِسْبَتُهُ أنه أصل العلوم، وما سواه فرغ. وواضعة: أبو الحَسَنِ الأَشْعَرِيُّ ومُتَابِعُوه، وأبو منصور المَاتُرِيدِيُّ ومتابعوه. واسمُهُ عِلْمُ التوحيد، وعلم الكلام، وذكر بعضُهم أن له ثمانية أسماء. واستمداده من الأدلة العقلية والنقلية. وحكم الشارع فيه الوجوب العيني على كلِّ مُكَلَّف من ذَكَرٍ وأنثى. ومسائله: قضاياه الباحِثَةُ عن الواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات.
Its subject is the essence of Allah and the essence of His messenger, in terms of what is necessary, what is impossible, and what is permissible; and the contingent thing in terms of being used as evidence for the existence of its Maker; and the transmitted matters (sam'iyyat) in terms of believing in them. Its fruit is knowledge of the attributes of Allah and His messengers by decisive proofs and attainment of eternal happiness. Its virtue is that it is the noblest of sciences because it is related to the essence of Allah Most High and the essence of His messengers and what follows that, and the thing related (al-muta'allaq) is ennobled by the nobility of that to which it is related (al-muta'allaq bihi). Its relation is that it is the foundation of the sciences, and everything else is subsidiary. Its founder is Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his followers, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers. Its name is 'ilm al-tawhid (the science of divine unity) and 'ilm al-kalam (the science of speech), and some mentioned that it has eight names. Its derivation is from rational and transmitted proofs. The ruling of the Lawgiver concerning it is individual obligation upon every legally responsible person, male and female. Its issues are its propositions that investigate the necessary, the permissible, and the impossible.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a definition and characterization of 'ilm al-kalam. It begins by stating the subject matter (al-mawdu'): the essence of Allah and the essence of His messenger, under the aspects of what is necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and permissible (ja'iz) regarding them. It also includes contingent things (mumkinat) as evidence for the existence of the Creator, and transmitted matters (sam'iyyat) as objects of belief. The fruit (thamara) of this science is knowledge of the attributes of Allah and His messengers through decisive proofs (barahin qat'iyya) and thereby attaining eternal happiness. Its virtue (fadl) is that it is the noblest of sciences because its object of study—the essence of Allah and His messengers—is most noble, and a science is ennobled by its object. Its relation (nisba) to other sciences is that it is the foundation (asl) and all others are subsidiary (far'). The founder (wadi') is identified as Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his followers, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers. It has names such as 'ilm al-tawhid and 'ilm al-kalam, with some claiming eight names. Its sources (istimdad) are rational (aqliyya) and transmitted (naqliyya) proofs. The legal ruling (hukm) regarding it is individual obligation (wajib 'ayni) upon every morally responsible person, male and female. Finally, its issues (masa'il) are its propositions that investigate the three categories: necessary, permissible, and impossible.

Key Terms
موضوع
ثمرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think kalam only studies God's essence.
Correction: Kalam also studies the Prophet, contingent evidence, and transmitted beliefs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'ilm al-kalam study?
A) Only God's essence
B) God's essence, the Prophet, contingent things, and transmitted matters
C) Only rational arguments
D) Only the Prophet's attributes

Key Takeaway
The subject of kalam is comprehensive: Allah, His messenger, contingency as proof, and revelation as belief; its fruit is certainty and eternal happiness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the fruit of kalam is both decisive knowledge and eternal happiness. Which of these two are you truly seeking in your study of this subject—are you pursuing certainty or just information? What would change if you treated every lesson as a step toward that eternal happiness?
?
The subject of kalam includes the essence of the messenger. Do you know and reflect on the necessary attributes of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) with the same seriousness as you consider Allah's attributes? How does that knowledge affect your love and obedience to him?
?
This passage states that contingent things are evidence for the existence of the Creator. When you look at the universe, do you actually use it as evidence to strengthen your conviction, or do you take it for granted? What one created thing today can you consciously reflect on as proof of Allah's existence?

The Virtue, Relation, and Founders of 'Ilm al-Kalam
Sanusi describes the virtue, relation, and founders of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the unique status of kalam as the noblest and foundational science, and learn its founders.

Core Idea
Kalam is the noblest science because its subject is noble; it is the root of all other sciences.

After defining the subject and benefit, Sanusi explains why kalam holds the highest rank among the Islamic sciences. Its virtue stems from its noble object of study, and its relation to other sciences is that of root to branch. He also identifies the founding Imams of the two great schools: al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the segment on virtue (fadl), relation (nisba), and founder (wadi').
Notice the phrase 'ashraf al-ulum' (noblest of sciences).
2
Understand why kalam is noble
The virtue comes from its subject: the essence of Allah and His messengers. Reflect on how a science's nobility is tied to its object.
3
Understand its foundational role
Kalam is the foundation (asl) of all other sciences; everything else is subsidiary (far'). Consider what this means for a student.
4
Know the founders
The two main founders are Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, along with their followers.
These are the two schools of Sunni kalam.

The Name, Sources, Ruling, and Issues of 'Ilm al-Kalam
Sanusi concludes with the names, sources, ruling, and issues of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the various names of kalam, its sources, its legal obligation, and the types of issues it investigates.

Core Idea
Kalam has many names, uses reason and revelation, is obligatory on every Muslim, and studies necessary, permissible, and impossible.

In the final part of his definition, Sanusi covers the remaining characteristics: the names by which this science is known, its methodological sources (both rational and transmitted), the legal ruling that it is an individual obligation, and the three categories of issues it examines. This completes the picture of what kalam is and why it is essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read from 'wa ismuhu' to the end. Notice the mention of eight names.
2
Learn the names
The primary names are 'ilm al-tawhid and 'ilm al-kalam. Some scholars count eight names.
Other names include 'ilm al-usul, 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat, etc.
3
Understand the sources
Kalam derives from both rational proofs (aqliyya) and transmitted proofs (naqliyya). Remember that reason and revelation complement each other.
4
Grasp the ruling
Learning kalam is fard 'ayn for every mature Muslim, male and female. This shows its importance.
5
Identify the issues
The issues (masa'il) are propositions about the necessary, permissible, and impossible. This echoes the categories mentioned earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Classification of Judgments: Rational, Customary, and Legal
Sanusi classifies judgments and justifies focusing on rational judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the threefold division of judgments and why kalam focuses exclusively on rational judgment.

Core Idea
Kalam needs only rational judgment; customary and legal belong to other sciences.

Sanusi begins by clarifying why he only discusses rational judgment: it is the one required for theological reasoning. He then presents the threefold classification of judgment in itself. This lesson unpacks that classification and the rationale for focusing on rationality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Sanusi first states his focus on rational judgment and then gives the general division.
The passage includes glosses; focus on the core matn.
2
Identify the three judgments
List the three types: rational (عقلي), customary (عادي), and legal (شرعي). Understand that this is a division of judgment in itself, not tied to any specific type.
The phrase 'من حيث هو' means 'in itself' regardless of specific type.
3
Understand why rational is singled out
Sanusi says he only discusses rational judgment because it is the one needed in the science of kalam. The other two are studied elsewhere.
This shows the scope of kalam as a discipline.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
Reflect on how this classification sets the stage for later discussions on what is rationally necessary, possible, and impossible for Allah.
This is foundational for all arguments in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن الحكم العقلي إنما اقتصر المصنف على الحكم العقلي دون أخويه وهما الحكم العادي والحكم الشرعي؛ لأنه المحتاج إليه في هذا الفن دونهما وحاصل الأمر أن أقسام الحكم من حيث هو ثلاثة:
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري.
(قوله: من حيث هو الخبر محذوف تقديره موجود أي: بقطع النظر عن كونه عقليا مثلا لئلا يلزم تقسيم الشيء إلى نفسه وإلى غيره.
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي
(قوله: أن أقسام الحكم من حيث هو ثلاثة... إلخ) يفيد أن الحكم الشرعي داخل تحت الحكم بمعنى إثبات أمر لأمر أو نفيه عنه، وكذا قوله: (ولا وضع واضع) يفيد ذلك، فإنه احترز به عن الحكم الشرعي، فيفيد أنه داخل في قوله: (إثبات أمر لأمر أو نفيه عنه)، وإلا لم يحتج لإخراجه بما ذكر، مع أنه سيأتي له أن الحكم الشرعي: هو كلام الله؛
That the rational judgment – the author limited himself to the rational judgment without its two brothers, which are the customary judgment and the legal judgment; because it is the one needed in this art, unlike them. And the conclusion is that the divisions of judgment in itself are three:
Hashiya of al-Allama Ahmad al-Ajhuri.
(His saying: 'in itself' – the predicate is omitted, its assumed meaning is 'existing', i.e., regardless of it being rational, for example, lest it necessitate dividing the thing into itself and other than itself.
Taqrirat of al-Allama Muhammad al-Anbabi.
(His saying: 'that the divisions of judgment in itself are three... etc.') It indicates that the legal judgment falls under judgment in the sense of affirming something of something or negating it from it, and likewise his saying: 'and no positor posited' indicates that; for he guarded against the legal judgment by that, so it indicates that it falls under his saying: 'affirming something of something or negating it from it', otherwise he would not have needed to exclude it by what was mentioned, especially since it will come from him that the legal judgment is the speech of Allah;
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a classification of judgments (hukm) into three types: rational, customary, and legal. The author explains that he only mentions rational judgment in this art of kalam because it is the one needed here, while the other two are discussed in other sciences. The commentary elaborates that the phrase 'in itself' means regardless of any specific type, to avoid dividing a thing into itself and something else. Further, it clarifies that the legal judgment falls under the general definition of judgment as affirmation or negation, and the author's phrase 'and no positor posited' is an exclusion to show that legal judgment is distinct yet still within the general definition, as it is the speech of Allah.

Key Terms
حكم عقلي
حكم عادي
حكم شرعي
أقسام الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That rational judgment is the only type of judgment
Correction: In fact, judgment is threefold: rational, customary, and legal. Kalam focuses on rational judgment, but the other two exist.

Checkpoint
Why does the author (Sanusi) only discuss rational judgment in this work?
A) Because it is the only valid judgment.
B) Because it is the only one needed in the science of kalam.
C) Because customary and legal judgments are not real.
D) Because the work is about law, not theology.

Key Takeaway
Kalam focuses on rational judgment, but judgment itself is threefold: rational, customary, and legal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the existence and oneness of Allah, is your conviction rooted in rational proof that you have personally examined, or are you relying on what you grew up believing? This lesson emphasizes that kalam focuses on rational judgment—so what is the basis of your faith? Ask yourself honestly, and if it is not rational, what steps can you take to build a conviction that is truly your own and based on evidence?
?
In your daily life, consider a recent religious decision you made. Did you base it on a rational analysis of evidence, on what is customary in your community, or on a legal ruling you heard? The author limited this science to rational judgment because it is what is needed—but are you neglecting rational judgment in your own practice? Set a commitment today to examine one of your core beliefs using rational proof from the sources.

What Is Kalam?
intermediate

The Definition of Legal Judgment and the Objection
Sanusi defines legal judgment and answers the objection to its definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defines legal judgment as God's speech and how he resolves the objection that God's speech is not an affirmation or negation.

Core Idea
Legal judgment is God's speech, not an affirmation—it is implicitly affirmative or a different convention.

Sanusi begins by defining the third category of judgment: legal judgment. He states it is God's speech related to human action. But a challenge arises: in kalam, a judgment is an affirmation or negation; God's speech is eternal words, not a mental assertion. How then can it be a judgment? Sanusi offers two clarifying answers. Let's read the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic sentence defining legal judgment. Note the key terms: الحكم الشرعي, كلام الله, متعلق بفعل الشخص, التكليف, الوضع.
2
Identify the objection
The text says 'إن قيل: إن كلام الله ليس إثبات أمر لأمر...'. Understand why someone might object that God's speech does not fit the pattern of a judgment.
The objection is that God's speech is not an act of affirming or denying something of something, as rational judgment is.
3
Study the two answers
The first answer invokes necessary consequence: God's command implies our affirmation of obligation. The second answer points to different terminology in uṣūl al-fiqh.
The second answer distinguishes between the uṣūlī definition (God's speech) and the fuqahā's definition (affirmation/negation by legal proof).
4
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how Sanusi shows that legal judgment can still be a 'judgment' even if not a direct affirmation, either by implication or by convention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالثُ : الحكم الشرعى وهو كلامُ الله المتعلق بفعل الشخص من حيث التكليف أو الوضع له.
(قوله: وَهُوَ كَلَامُ الله ... إلخ) إن قيل: إن كلام الله ليس إثبات أمر لأمر... إلخ؛ فالجواب بأحد أمرين: الأول: أنه إثبات باعتبار لازمه ؛ لأن كلام الله الذي اقتضى الطلب على وجه الجزم يتضمن إثباتنا الوجوب .وهكذا الثاني: أن تعريف الحكم الشرعي بما ذکر اصطلاح للأصوليين، واصطلاح الفقهاء أن الحكم الشرعي: إثبات أمر لأمر أو نفيه عنه بواسطة الدليل الشرعي.
(قوله: الْمُتَعَلَّقُ بِفِعْل الشَّخْصِ) أي: الدال عليه.
(قوله: مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّكْلِيف :أي لا من حيث إنه مخلوق أو ممكن مثلاً، ومراده بالتكليف ما يعم الطلب بأقسامه الأربعة والإباحة.
(وقوله: أوِ الْوَضْع لَهُ أي للتكليف الشامل للطلب بأقسامه الأربعة وللإباحة ومعنى الوضع لذلك: جعل الشارع لذلك سبباً أو شرطاً أو مانعاً وإثباته الصحة إن استوفى الأمور المعتبرة فيه والفساد إن لم يستوفها، فالطلب بأقسامه الأربعة والإباحة والوضع بالمعنى المتقدم مدلولة للكلام كما يعلم من "حاشية الهدهدي" وإن كان الكلام نفسه طلباً وإباحة ووضعاً باعتبار دلالته عليها كما يعلم أيضاً من الحاشية المذكورة، والظاهر أن إطلاق الطلب والإباحة والوضع على الكلام باعتبار تلك الدلالة مجازي من إطلاق اسم المدلول على الدال إلا أن يكونوا اصطلحوا على ذلك الإطلاق، فيكون إطلاقاً حقيقياً.
(قوله: (الْمُتَعَلَّقُ) أي: تعلّق دِلالةٍ، لا تأثير ولا انكشاف، والمراد: تعلقاً تنجيزياً حادثاً عند توجه الطلب، ولا يلزم من حدوث التعلق الذي هو صِفَةُ الكلام حدوث الحُكْمِ المفسر بالكلام المذكور؛ لأن التعلُّق المذكور ليس صِفَةً حقيقة، بل هو نِسْبَةٌ واعتبار، فلا يلزم من حدوثها حدوث موصوفها، فالحكم قديم لا حادث، وذهب العلامة المَحَلِّي إلى حدوثه.
And the third: the legal judgment: it is the speech of God related to the action of a person in terms of obligation or stipulation for it. (His saying: 'And it is the speech of God... etc.') If it is said: 'The speech of God is not affirmation of a matter for a matter... etc.,' then the answer is with one of two things: the first: that it is affirmation in consideration of its necessary consequence, because the speech of God that necessitated the request in a decisive manner includes our affirmation of obligation. Similarly, the second: that the definition of the legal judgment as mentioned is a terminology of the uṣūliyyūn, and the terminology of the fuqahā' is that the legal judgment is the affirmation of a matter for a matter or the negation of it from it by means of a legal proof. (His saying: 'related to the action of a person') i.e., indicating it. (His saying: 'in terms of obligation') i.e., not in terms of it being created or possible, for example, and his intention by obligation is what includes the request in its four divisions and permission. (And his saying: 'or stipulation for it') i.e., for the obligation that includes the request in its four divisions and permission; and the meaning of stipulation for that is: the Lawgiver's making for that a cause, or a condition, or an impediment, and His affirming its validity if it fulfills the considerations and its invalidity if it does not fulfill them. So the request in its four divisions, permission, and stipulation in the aforementioned sense are the meanings indicated by the speech, as is known from 'Hashiyat al-Hudhdhī', even if the speech itself is request, permission, and stipulation in consideration of its indication of them, as is also known from the aforementioned hashya. And the apparent is that the application of request, permission, and stipulation to speech in consideration of that indication is metaphorical, from applying the name of the indicated to the indicator, unless they have made it a conventional application, in which case it would be literal. (His saying: 'the related') i.e., a relation of indication, not of effect nor of disclosure, and what is meant is an actualized relation that occurs when the request is directed; and the occurrence of the relation, which is an attribute of speech, does not necessitate the occurrence of the judgment interpreted as the mentioned speech, because the mentioned relation is not a real attribute, but rather a relation and consideration, so its occurrence does not necessitate the occurrence of its qualified; thus the judgment is eternal, not temporal, and al-ʿAllāma al-Maḥallī went to its temporality.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines legal judgment (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī) and discusses several important points. Sanusi defines it as God's speech (kalām Allāh) relating to a person's act in terms of taklīf (obligation) or waḍʿ (stipulation). The commentary first addresses a potential objection: God's speech is not itself an affirmation or negation (as in the rational judgment), so how can it be a 'judgment'? Two answers are given: (1) God's speech that commands or prohibits necessarily implies our affirmation of obligation, so it is affirmation by necessary consequence; (2) jurists (fuqahā') define legal judgment differently—as affirmation or negation by a legal proof, which is a different convention. Then al-Ajhuri explains that 'related to the action of a person' means indicating it, and 'in terms of obligation' excludes considering the act as mere creation or possibility. Obligation here includes the four types of request (command, prohibition, etc.) and permission (ibāḥa). 'Stipulation' means the Lawgiver designates something as a cause, condition, or impediment, and declares validity or invalidity. The commentary notes that the terms 'request', 'permission', and 'stipulation' are applied to God's speech metaphorically in terms of their indication, unless conventionalized. Finally, al-Anbābī's gloss explains that the relation (taʿalluq) of God's speech to human acts is a relation of indication, not of causation; it occurs temporally when the request is directed, but this does not entail that the judgment itself (which is the speech) is temporal, because the relation is not a real attribute. Therefore, the judgment (God's speech) is eternal, though al-Maḥallī held it to be temporal. This touches on the kalām debate about the eternality of God's speech.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي
كلام الله
إثبات
نفي
الأصوليون
الفقهاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That legal judgment must be a direct affirmation or negation in the mind, like rational judgment.
Correction: Legal judgment as God's speech is a different kind: it is either implicitly affirmative (by necessary consequence) or defined by a different convention (uṣūl al-fiqh).

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, how does God's speech constitute an affirmation?
A) It is directly an affirmation of obligation
B) It implies our affirmation of obligation
C) It is an affirmation by the jurists' definition
D) It is not an affirmation at all

Key Takeaway
Sanusi answers the objection that God's speech is not an affirmation by showing it is implicitly affirmative or part of a different convention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a religious command that feels demanding or inconvenient, do you tend to dismiss it as a human construct? How does Sanusi's insistence that God's speech necessarily implies your affirmation of obligation challenge that tendency? Will you commit today to seeing every divine command as carrying a personal claim on your obedience?
?
Sanusi presents two conventions for defining legal judgment—one focusing on God's speech, the other on human affirmation. Which definition have you been unconsciously using in your own life? How would your practice of Islam change if you consistently treated God's speech as the foundation of every ruling, not just a human scholarly opinion?
?
The objector claimed God's speech is not an affirmation, perhaps to avoid the burden of obligation. Are there areas of your life where you have used intellectual objections to justify disobedience or indifference to Islamic rulings? What would it mean for you to accept that God's commands carry an inescapable affirmation that demands action?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate

Understanding Taklīf and Waḍʿ in Legal Judgment
Al-Ajhuri explains taklīf and waḍʿ in detail and discusses the application of terms to God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the terms 'taklīf' and 'waḍʿ' in the definition of legal judgment, including the four types of request, permission, and the Lawgiver's stipulative acts.

Core Idea
Taklīf includes all four demands and permission; waḍʿ refers to cause, condition, impediment, validity, and invalidity.

Sanusi's definition of legal judgment includes the terms 'taklīf' (obligation) and 'waḍʿ' (stipulation). Al-Ajhuri's commentary expands these terms greatly. He explains that 'taklīf' here is broad, covering command, prohibition, recommendation, and discouragement, plus permission. 'Waḍʿ' refers to the Lawgiver designating something as a cause, condition, or impediment, and declaring acts valid or invalid. Moreover, the commentary clarifies that these terms are applied to God's speech by indication, often metaphorically. Let's study the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition phrase
Focus on the phrase 'المتعلق بفعل الشخص من حيث التكليف أو الوضع له' and its explanation. Understand that 'related' means 'indicating' the act.
2
Grasp the scope of taklīf
Al-Ajhuri says taklīf includes the four types of request and permission. Identify these: command, prohibition, recommendation, discouragement, and permissibility.
This broadens taklīf beyond mere obligation.
3
Understand waḍʿ
Waḍʿ means the Lawgiver's making something a cause, condition, or impediment, and affirming validity or invalidity. This is about the stipulations of acts.
Examples: prayer requires purification (cause), conditions like facing qibla, impediments like menstruation.
4
Note the metaphorical application
The commentary says calling God's speech 'request', 'permission', or 'stipulation' is metaphorical, referring to its indication, unless conventionalized.
This avoids anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
